2:19:963:0:14:72:397:700:12:Times:12:Times:C:Estimating Dynamic Equilibrium Models with Stochastic Volatility
2:20:1027:14:14:72:469:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:Jesus Fernandez-Villaverde, Pablo A. Guerrón-Quintana, and Juan Rubio-Ramírez
2:21:1104:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:NBER Working Paper No. 18399
2:22:1132:14:14:72:150:658:12:Times:12:Times:C:September 2012
2:23:1146:14:28:72:151:644:12:Times:12:Times:C:JEL No. C1,E30
2:24:1160:28:28:306:339:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:25:1168:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:C:We propose a novel method to estimate dynamic equilibrium models with stochastic volatility. First,
2:26:1267:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:C:we characterize the properties of the solution to this class of models. Second, we take advantage of
2:27:1367:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:C:the results about the structure of the solution to build a sequential Monte Carlo algorithm to evaluate
2:28:1470:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:C:the likelihood function of the model. The approach, which exploits the profusion of shocks in stochastic
2:29:1574:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:C:volatility models, is versatile and computationally tractable even in large-scale models, such as those
2:30:1677:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:C:often employed by policy-making institutions. As an application, we use our algorithm and Bayesian
2:31:1775:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:C:methods to estimate a business cycle model of the U.S. economy with both stochastic volatility and
2:32:1873:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:C:parameter drifting in monetary policy. Our application shows the importance of stochastic volatility
2:33:1973:14:42:72:277:476:12:Times:12:Times:C:in accounting for the dynamics of the data.
2:34:2016:42:14:72:205:434:12:Times:12:Times:C:Jesus Fernandez-Villaverde
2:35:2042:14:14:72:203:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:University of Pennsylvania
2:36:2068:14:14:72:175:406:12:Times:12:Times:C:160 McNeil Building
2:37:2087:14:14:72:161:392:12:Times:12:Times:C:3718 Locust Walk
2:38:2103:14:14:72:186:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:Philadelphia, PA 19104
2:39:2125:14:14:72:124:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:40:2133:14:28:72:192:350:12:Times:12:Times:C:jesusfv@econ.upenn.edu
2:41:2155:28:14:72:205:322:12:Times:12:Times:C:Pablo A. Guerrón-Quintana
2:42:2180:14:14:72:254:308:12:Times:12:Times:C:Federal Reserve Bank of Philadelphia
2:43:2216:14:0:72:205:294:12:Times:12:Times:C:pablo.guerron@phil.frb.org
2:44:2242:0:14:306:405:434:12:Times:12:Times:C:Juan Rubio-Ramírez
2:45:2260:14:14:306:386:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:Duke University
2:46:2275:14:14:306:383:406:12:Times:12:Times:C:P.O. Box 90097
2:47:2289:14:14:306:401:392:12:Times:12:Times:C:Durham, NC 27708
2:48:2305:14:0:306:450:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:juan.rubio-ramirez@duke.edu
3:49:2332:0:33:58:165:721:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:1. Introduction
3:50:2347:33:22:58:553:688:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Over the last few years, economists have uncovered the importance of time-varying volatility in
3:51:2442:22:22:58:553:666:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:accounting for the dynamics of U.S. aggregate data. Stock and Watson (2002) and Sims and
3:52:2530:22:21:58:553:644:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Zha (2006) are some prominent examples of this line of research.  As a response, a growing
3:53:2620:21:22:58:553:623:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:literature has developed to investigate the origins and consequences of time-varying volatility. A
3:54:2718:22:22:58:553:601:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:particularly successful branch of this literature uses dynamic equilibrium models to emphasize the
3:55:2816:22:22:58:553:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:role of volatility shocks (also known as uncertainty shocks, but in any case speciÖed as stochastic
3:56:2915:22:21:58:553:557:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:volatility as in Shephard, 2008) in business cycle áuctuations. Among those we can highlight are
3:57:3011:21:22:58:553:536:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Bloomet al.(2007), Fern·ndez-Villaverde and Rubio-RamÌrez (2007), Justiniano and Primiceri
3:58:3101:22:22:58:553:514:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(2008), Bloom (2009), Fern·ndez-Villaverdeet al.(2010c), and Bloomet al.(2012). In these
3:59:3189:22:21:58:553:492:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:models, there are two types of shocks: structural shocks (shock to productivity, to preferences,
3:60:3285:21:22:58:553:471:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to policy, etc.) and volatility shocks (shocks to the standard deviation of the innovations to the
3:61:3383:22:22:58:153:449:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:structural shocks).
3:62:3402:22:21:76:553:427:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:To fulÖll the promise in this literature, it is crucial to have a set of tools to take these dynamic
3:63:3502:21:22:58:553:406:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium models with stochastic volatility to the data. Namely, we want to estimate, evaluate,
3:64:3599:22:22:58:553:384:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and compare these models using a likelihood-based approach. However, the task is complicated
3:65:3691:22:21:58:553:362:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:by the inherent non-linearity that stochastic volatility generates. By construction, linearization is
3:66:3792:21:22:58:553:341:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ill-equipped to handle time-varying volatility models because it yields certainty-equivalent policy
3:67:3891:22:22:58:553:319:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:functions. That is, volatility ináuences neither the agentsídecision rules nor the laws of motion
3:68:3988:22:21:58:553:297:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of the aggregate variables. Hence, to consider how volatility a§ects those, it becomes imperative
3:69:4085:21:22:58:553:276:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to employ a non-linear solution method for the dynamics of the economy.  Once we consider
3:70:4174:22:22:58:543:254:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:non-linear solution methods we are forced to use simulation-based estimators of the likelihood.
3:71:4269:22:21:76:554:232:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:In principle, and beyond the computational burden, this could seem a mild challenge. For
3:72:4357:21:22:58:553:211:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:instance, one could be tempted to get around this problem by solving the model non-linearly with
3:73:4453:22:22:58:553:189:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a fast algorithm and employing, for estimation, a particle Ölter to get an unbiased simulation-
3:74:4548:22:21:58:553:167:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:based estimator of the likelihood. The particle Ölter presented in Fern·ndez-Villaverde and Rubio-
3:75:4646:21:22:58:553:146:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:RamÌrez (2007) would be a natural candidate for such an undertaking. Unfortunately, that version
3:76:4742:22:22:58:553:124:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of the particle Ölter relies, when estimating models with stochastic volatility, on the presence of lin-
3:77:4846:22:21:58:553:102:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ear measurement errors in observables. Otherwise, we would be forced to solve a large quadratic
3:78:4941:21:22:58:553:81:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:system of equations with multiple solutions, an endeavor for which there are no suitable algo-
3:79:5035:22:0:58:553:59:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:rithms. Although measurement errors are both plausible and empirically relevant, their presence
4:80:5131:0:22:58:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:complicates the interpretation of the results. Thus, it is desirable to consider a particle Ölter that
4:81:5233:22:21:58:281:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:departs from requiring measurement errors.
4:82:5275:21:22:76:553:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:To accomplish this goal, we show how to write a particle Ölter that allows us to evaluate
4:83:5364:22:22:58:553:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the likelihood of a dynamic equilibrium model with stochastic volatility by exploiting the struc-
4:84:5461:22:21:58:553:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ture of the second-order approximation to the decision rules that characterize the equilibrium
4:85:5555:21:22:58:553:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of the economy without the need of measurement errors. Second-order approximations capture
4:86:5645:22:22:58:553:591:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the implications of stochastic volatility and are convenient because they are accurate but not
4:87:5739:22:21:58:197:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:computationally expensive.
4:88:5765:21:22:76:554:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We achieve the objective in two steps. First, we characterize the second-order approximation
4:89:5857:22:22:58:552:526:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:B:to the decision rules of a rather general dynamic equilibrium model with stochastic volatility.1
4:90:5953:22:21:58:553:504:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Second, we demonstrate how we can use this characterization to handily simulate the likelihood
4:91:6047:21:22:58:553:483:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:function of the model with a particle Ölter without measurement errors. The key is to show how
4:92:6141:22:22:58:553:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the decision rules characterization reduces the quadratic problem associated with the evaluation
4:93:6237:22:21:58:553:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of the approximated measurement density to a much simpler matrix inversion problem. This is a
4:94:6330:21:22:58:553:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:novel extension of sequential Monte Carlo methods that can be useful for other applications. After
4:95:6428:22:22:58:553:396:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:we have evaluated the likelihood, we can combine it with a prior and an Markov chain Monte
4:96:6518:22:21:58:538:374:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Carlo (McMc) algorithm to draw from the posterior distribution (Flury and Shephard, 2011).
4:97:6608:21:22:76:553:353:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Our characterization of the second-order approximation to the decision rules should be of
4:98:6697:22:22:58:553:331:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:interest in itself even for researchers who are not evaluating the likelihood of their model but who
4:99:6797:22:21:58:553:309:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:are keen to understand how the model works. Among others, the results are useful to analyze the
4:100:6892:21:22:58:553:288:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium of the model, to explore the shape of its impulse-response functions, or to calibrate
4:101:6989:22:22:58:69:266:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:it.
4:102:6992:22:34:76:238:244:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:More concretely, we prove that:
4:103:7023:34:22:72:553:210:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:1. The Örst-order approximation to the decision rules of the agents (or any other equilibrium
4:104:7116:22:32:87:545:188:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:object of interest) does not depend on volatility shocks and they are certainty equivalent.
4:105:7207:32:21:72:553:156:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:2. The second-order approximation to the decision rules of the agents only depends on volatility
4:106:7303:21:22:87:553:135:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:shocks on terms where volatility is multiplied by the innovation to its own structural shock.
4:107:7396:22:28:87:553:113:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:For instance, if we have two structural shocks (a productivity and a preference shock) and
4:108:7486:28:15:71:553:85:7:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:F:1These theorems generalize previous results derived by Schmitt-GrohÈ and Uribe (2004), for the homoscedastic
4:109:7594:15:0:58:218:70:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:F:shocks case to the time-varying case.
5:110:7632:0:22:87:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:a volatility shock to each of them, the only non-zero term where the volatility shock to
5:111:7720:22:21:87:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:productivity appears is the one where the volatility shock to productivity multiplies the
5:112:7809:21:22:87:553:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:innovation to the productivity shock. Thus, of the terms in the second-order approximation
5:113:7899:22:32:87:506:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:that complicate the evaluation of the likelihood function, only a few are non-zero.
5:114:7982:32:21:72:553:624:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:3. The perturbation parameter will only appear in a non-zero term where it is raised to a
5:115:8071:21:35:87:543:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:square. This term is a constant that corrects for precautionary behavior induced by risk.
5:116:8160:35:22:76:553:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:As an application, we estimate a dynamic equilibrium model of the U.S. economy with stochas-
5:117:8252:22:21:58:553:546:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tic volatility using the particle Ölter and Bayesian methods. The model, an otherwise standard
5:118:8346:21:22:58:553:525:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:business cycle model with nominal rigidities, incorporates not only stochastic volatility in the
5:119:8442:22:22:58:553:503:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shocks that drive its dynamics but also parameter drifting in the parameters that control mone-
5:120:8537:22:21:58:553:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tary policy. In that way, we include two of the main mechanisms that researchers have highlighted
5:121:8634:21:22:58:553:460:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to account for the time-varying volatility of U.S. data: heteroscedastic shocks and parameter drift-
5:122:8734:22:22:58:553:438:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ing. We include these together in the model because a ìone-at-a-timeî investigation is fraught
5:123:8828:22:21:58:553:416:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:with peril. If we allow only one source of variation in the model, the likelihood may want to take
5:124:8926:21:22:58:553:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:advantage of this extra degree of áexibility to Öt the data better. For example, if the ìtrueîmodel
5:125:9025:22:22:58:553:373:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is one with parameter drifting in monetary policy, an estimated model without drift but with sto-
5:126:9122:22:21:58:553:351:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:chastic volatility in one of the structural shocks may interpret the ìtrueî drift as time-varying
5:127:9219:21:22:58:553:330:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:volatility in that shock. If, instead, we had time-varying volatility in technological shocks in the
5:128:9319:22:22:58:553:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:data, an estimated model without stochastic volatility and only parameter drifting may conclude,
5:129:9415:22:21:58:553:286:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:erroneously, that the parameters of monetary policy are changing. Lastly, we have a model that
5:130:9509:21:22:58:553:265:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is as rich as the models employed by policy-making institutions in real life. While solving and
5:131:9604:22:22:58:553:243:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:estimating such a large model is a computational challenge, we wanted to demonstrate that our
5:132:9697:22:21:58:553:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:procedure is of practical use and to make our application a blueprint for the estimation of other
5:133:9794:21:22:58:206:200:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:dynamic equilibrium models.
5:134:9821:22:22:76:553:178:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Our main empirical Öndings are as follows. First, the posterior distribution of parameters
5:135:9911:22:21:58:553:156:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:puts most of its mass in areas that denote a fair amount of stochastic volatility, yet another
5:136:10005:21:22:58:553:135:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:proof of the importance of time-varying volatility in applied models. Second, a model comparison
5:137:10101:22:22:58:553:113:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:exercise indicates that, even after controlling for stochastic volatility, the data clearly prefer a
5:138:10201:22:21:58:553:91:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:speciÖcation where monetary policy changes over time. This Önding should not be interpreted,
5:139:10293:21:0:58:553:70:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:though, as implying that volatility shocks did not play a role of their own. It means, instead,
6:140:10389:0:22:58:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that a successful model of the U.S. economy requires the presence of both stochastic volatility
6:141:10484:22:21:58:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and parameter drifting, a result that challenges the results of Sims and Zha (2006). Finally, we
6:142:10580:21:22:58:553:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:document the evolution of the structural shocks, of stochastic volatility, and the parameters of
6:143:10676:22:22:58:553:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monetary policy. We emphasize the conáuence, during the 1970s, of times of high volatility and
6:144:10770:22:21:58:553:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:weak responses to ináation, and, during the 1990s, of positive structural shocks and low volatility
6:145:10869:21:22:58:553:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:even if monetary policy was weaker than often argued. In the appendix, we thoroughly explore
6:146:10961:22:22:58:553:591:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the model, including the construction of counterfactual histories of the U.S. data by varying
6:147:11054:22:21:58:553:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:some aspect of the model such as shutting down time-varying volatility or imposing alternative
6:148:11148:21:22:58:151:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monetary policies.
6:149:11166:22:22:76:553:526:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:An alternative to our stochastic volatility framework would be to work with Markov regime-
6:150:11256:22:21:58:553:504:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:switching models such as those of Bianchi (2009) or Farmeret al.(2009). This class of models
6:151:11348:21:22:58:553:483:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:provides an extra degree of áexibility in modelling aggregate dynamics that is highly promising.
6:152:11444:22:22:58:553:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:In fact, some of the fast changes in policy parameters that we document in our empirical sec-
6:153:11537:22:21:58:553:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tion suggest that discrete jumps could be a good representation of the data. However, current
6:154:11630:21:22:58:553:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:technical limitations regarding the computation of the equilibria induced by regime switches force
6:155:11728:22:22:58:518:396:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:researchers to focus on small models that are only stylized representations of an economy.
6:156:11818:22:21:76:553:374:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, even if the motivation for our approach and the application belong to macroeconomics,
6:157:11912:21:22:58:553:353:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:there is nothing speciÖc about that Öeld in the tools we present. One can think about the impor-
6:158:12008:22:22:58:553:331:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tance of estimating dynamic equilibrium models with stochastic volatility in many other Öelds,
6:159:12102:22:21:58:553:309:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:from Önance (Bansal and Yaron, 2004, would be a prominent example) to industrial organization
6:160:12195:21:22:58:553:288:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(for instance, an equilibrium model of industry dynamics where the demand and supply shocks
6:161:12286:22:22:58:553:266:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:have time-varying volatility), international trade (where innovations to the real exchange rates or
6:162:12385:22:21:58:553:244:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the country spreads are well known to have time-varying volatility, see Fern·ndez-Villaverdeet
6:163:12482:21:22:58:199:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f2:B:al., 2010c), or many others.
6:164:12510:22:22:76:554:201:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The rest of the paper is organized as follows. Section 2 presents a generic dynamic equilibrium
6:165:12605:22:21:58:553:179:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:model with stochastic volatility to Öx notation and discuss how to solve it. Section 3 explains

6:167:12794:22:22:58:553:136:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:an application of our procedure, takes it to the U.S. data, and comments on the main Öndings.

10:275:18922:40:29:58:362:490:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:2.4. Approximating the State-Space Representation
10:276:18971:29:22:58:553:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:In general, when we deal with the class of dynamic equilibrium models with stochastic volatility,
10:277:19068:22:22:58:553:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:we do not have access to a closed-form solution, that is, the policy functionshandgcannot be

10:281:19394:22:21:76:553:352:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:There are many di§erent solution algorithms for dynamic equilibrium models. Among those,
10:282:19482:21:22:58:553:331:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the perturbation method has emerged as a popular way (see Judd and Guu, 1997, Schmitt-GrohÈ
10:283:19573:22:22:58:553:309:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and Uribe, 2004, and Aruobaet al., 2006 among others) to obtain higher-order Taylor series
10:284:19663:22:21:58:553:287:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:approximations to the policy functions (6)-(7) together with equations (4) and (5) around the
10:285:19756:21:22:58:553:266:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:steady state. It is key to note that we also get the Taylor expansion of (4) because it is a non-
10:286:19853:22:22:58:553:244:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:linear function. Beyond being extremely fast for systems with a large number of state variables,
10:287:19949:22:21:58:553:222:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:perturbation o§ers high levels of accuracy even relatively far away from the perturbation point
10:288:20044:21:22:58:485:201:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(Aruoba,et al., 2006, and, for cases with stochastic volatility, Caldaraet al., 2012).

15:663:27683:0:22:76:554:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Solving this system is non-trivial. Since the system is quadratic, we may have either none or
15:664:27776:22:21:58:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:several di§erent solutions. In fact, it is even hard to know how many solutions there are. But
15:665:27870:21:22:58:553:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:even if we knew the number of solutions, we are not aware of any accurate and e¢ cient method to
15:666:27966:22:22:58:553:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:solve quadratic problems that Önds all the solutions. This di¢ culty seemingly prevents us from
15:667:28061:22:21:58:343:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:achieving our goal of evaluating the likelihood function.
15:668:28118:21:22:76:554:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:A solution would be to introduce, as Fern·ndez-Villaverde and Rubio-RamÌrez (2007) did, a
15:669:28207:22:22:58:553:591:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f2:B:k-1vector of linear measurement errors and solve for those instead ofUt. In this case the system
15:670:28303:22:21:58:553:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:would have a unique, easy to Önd solution. However, there are three reasons, in increasing order
15:671:28399:21:35:58:322:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of importance, why this solution is not satisfactory:
15:672:28452:35:22:72:553:513:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:1. Although measurement errors are both plausible and empirically relevant, their presence
15:673:28542:22:21:87:553:491:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:complicates the interpretation of any empirical results.  In particular, we are interested
15:674:28632:21:22:87:553:470:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:in measuring how heteroscedastic structural shocks help in accounting for the data and
15:675:28718:22:32:87:278:448:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:measurement errors can confound us.
15:676:28753:32:21:72:553:416:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:2. The absence of measurement errors will help us to illustrate below how dynamic equilibrium
15:677:28846:21:32:87:553:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:models with volatility shocks have a profusion of shocks that we can exploit in our estimation.
15:678:28941:32:22:72:553:363:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:3. As we will also show below, volatility shocks would enter linearly (conditional on the draw)
15:679:29036:22:21:87:553:341:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:in the system equations. Since, by deÖnition, linear measurement errors would also enter in
15:680:29127:21:35:87:461:320:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:the same fashion, it would be hard to identify one apart from the others.
15:681:29200:35:22:76:553:285:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Our alternative in this paper is to realize that considering stochastic volatility converts the
15:682:29295:22:21:58:553:263:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:above-described quadratic system into a linear one. Hence, if a rank condition is satisÖed, the
15:683:29390:21:22:58:553:242:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:system (22) has only one solution and the solution can be found by simply inverting a matrix.
15:684:29483:22:22:58:553:220:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Thus, requirement 1 in assumption 1 holds and we can use the particle Ölter. The core of the
15:685:29575:22:21:58:553:198:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:argument is to note that, when volatility shocks are considered, the policy functions share a
15:686:29668:21:39:58:246:177:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:peculiar pattern that we can exploit.
15:687:29705:39:29:58:231:138:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:3.1. Structure of the Solution
15:688:29735:29:22:58:553:109:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Our Örst step will characterize the Örst- and second-order derivatives of the policy functions
15:689:29829:22:21:58:553:87:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f2:B:handgevaluated at the steady state. Then, we will describe an interesting pattern in these
15:690:29919:21:0:58:553:66:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:derivatives. The second step will take advantage of the pattern to show that, when the number
16:691:30014:0:22:58:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of volatility shocks equals the number of observables, our quadratic system becomes a linear one.
16:692:30111:22:21:58:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:This characterization is important both for estimation and, more generally, for the analysis of
16:693:30206:21:39:58:467:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:perturbation solutions to dynamic equilibrium models with stochastic volatility.

20:1130:37862:0:22:76:554:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Theorem 5 shows that requirement 1 in assumption 1 holds.  Consequently, we can use a
20:1131:37947:22:21:58:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:variation of the particle Ölter adapted for our class of dynamic equilibrium models with volatility
20:1132:38046:21:22:58:553:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:B:shocks. We are requiringB("it;\r)to be full rank. When canB("it;\r)not be full rank?B("it;\r)
20:1133:38139:22:22:58:553:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:would fail to have full rank when the impact of volatility innovations are identical across several
20:1134:38238:22:21:58:553:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:elements ofYt. This would mean that the observables lack enough information to tell volatility
20:1135:38332:21:22:58:553:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shocks apart. If this is the case, a new set of observables would have to be chosen to estimate the
20:1136:38431:22:22:58:92:591:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:model.
20:1137:38437:22:21:76:553:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Note also that theorem 5 assumesk=m.  Given the notation in section 2.1, this means

20:1139:38612:22:22:58:553:526:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:necessary. What the theorem needs is that the number of volatility shocks equals the number of
20:1140:38706:22:21:58:553:504:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:observables. Since, to simplify notation, we have assumed that all structural shocks face volatility
20:1141:38806:21:22:58:553:483:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shocks, the number of structural shocks equals the number of observables. As mentioned in section
20:1142:38903:22:22:58:553:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:2.1, we could have structural shocks that do not face volatility shocks (this will be the case in
20:1143:39000:22:21:58:553:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:our application to follow). In that case, we could have more structural shocks than observables.

21:1228:40712:44:34:58:553:417:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:4. An Application: A Business Cycle Model with Stochastic Volatility
21:1229:40780:34:22:58:553:383:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:As an illustration of our procedure, we estimate a business cycle model of the U.S. economy with
21:1230:40876:22:21:58:553:361:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:nominal rigidities and stochastic volatility. We will show: 1) how we can characterize posterior
21:1231:40972:21:22:58:553:340:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:distributions of the parameters of interest and 2) how we can recover and analyze the smoothed
21:1232:41066:22:22:58:553:318:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:structural and volatility shocks. Those are two of the most relevant exercises in terms of the
21:1233:41160:22:21:58:553:296:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:estimation of dynamic equilibrium models. Once the estimation has been undertaken, there are
21:1234:41252:21:22:58:553:275:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:many other exercises that can be done with the empirical results. For instance, in the appendix,
21:1235:41348:22:22:58:553:253:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:we include several of those such as: 1) Önding the impulse response functions (IRFs) of the model;
21:1236:41446:22:21:58:553:231:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:2) evaluating the Öt of the model in comparison with some alternatives; and 3) undertaking some
21:1237:41541:21:22:58:478:210:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:counterfactuals and run alternative histories of the evolution of the U.S. economy.
21:1238:41624:22:22:76:553:188:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Before doing so, though, we need to motivate our choice of application. The model that we
21:1239:41713:22:21:58:553:166:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:present has many strengths but also important weaknesses. Su¢ ce it to say here that since this
21:1240:41808:21:22:58:553:145:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:model is the base of much applied policy analysis by academics and policy-making institutions, it
21:1241:41905:22:22:58:553:123:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is a natural example for this paper. Thus, given that the model is well known, our presentation
21:1242:42000:22:21:58:553:101:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:will be brief. We will depart only along two dimensions from the standard model: we will have
21:1243:42093:21:22:58:553:80:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:stochastic volatility in the shocks that drive the dynamics of the economy (the object of interest
21:1244:42191:22:0:58:553:58:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in this paper) and parameter drifting in the monetary policy rule. In that way, the likelihood
22:1245:42287:0:22:58:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:has the chance of picking between two of the alternatives that the literature has highlighted to

22:1247:42480:21:22:58:553:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a reduced volatility of the shocks that hit the economy (as in Sims and Zha, 2006) or a di§erent

26:1487:51898:22:38:58:553:169:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:drift in the Taylor rule would disappear as well from the equilibrium dynamics (see appendix 6.3).
26:1488:51996:38:30:58:207:131:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:4.5. Data and Estimation
26:1489:52020:30:21:58:553:101:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:We estimate our model using the Öve time series for the U.S. economy described above. Our
26:1490:52109:21:22:58:553:80:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:sample covers 1959.Q1 to 2007.Q1, with 192 observations. Because of space considerations, we
26:1491:52201:22:0:58:553:58:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:stop at 2007 to avoid having to deal with the recent Önancial crisis, which would make it di¢ cult
27:1492:52301:0:22:58:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to appreciate the points we want to illustrate about how to econometrically deal with stochastic
27:1493:52397:22:21:58:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:volatility. This could be Öxed at the cost of a lengthier discussion. Appendix 6.5 explains how we
27:1494:52495:21:22:58:160:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:construct the series.
27:1495:52516:22:22:76:554:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Once we have evaluated the likelihood, we combine it with a prior. We pick áat priors on
27:1496:52604:22:21:58:553:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a bounded support for all the parameters. The bounds are either natural economic restrictions
27:1497:52697:21:22:58:553:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(for instance, the Calvo and indexation parameters lie between 0 and 1) or are so wide that
27:1498:52788:22:22:58:553:591:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the likelihood assigns (numerically) zero probability to values outside them. Bounded áat priors
27:1499:52884:22:21:58:421:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:induce a proper posterior, a convenient feature for our exercises below.
27:1500:52956:21:22:76:554:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We resort to áat priors for two reasons. First, to reduce the impact of presample information
27:1501:53049:22:22:58:553:526:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and show that our results arise mainly from the shape of the likelihood and not from the prior
27:1502:53143:22:21:58:553:504:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(although, of course, áat priors are not invariant to reparameterization). Thus, the reader who
27:1503:53238:21:22:58:553:483:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:wants to interpret our posterior modes as maximum likelihood point estimates can do so. Sec-
27:1504:53330:22:22:58:553:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ond, because as we learned in Fern·ndez-Villaverdeet al.(2010c), eliciting priors for stochastic
27:1505:53426:22:21:58:553:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:volatility is di¢ cult, since we deal with unfamiliar units, such as the variance of volatility shocks,
27:1506:53529:21:22:58:553:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:about which we do not have clear beliefs. Flat priors come, though, at a price: before proceeding
27:1507:53626:22:29:58:553:396:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to the estimation, we have to Öx several parameters to reduce the dimensionality of the problem.

27:1517:54379:22:21:58:553:166:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:models. We set the cost of capital utilization,\b2, to a small number to introduce some curvature
27:1518:54476:21:22:58:553:145:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in this decision. Three parameter values are borrowed from the point estimates from a similar
27:1519:54569:22:22:58:553:123:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:model without stochastic volatility or parameter drifting presented in Fern·ndez-Villaverdeet al.
27:1520:54666:22:21:58:553:101:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2009). The Örst is the inverse of the Frisch labor elasticity,#= 1:17. As argued by Chettyet
27:1521:54759:21:22:58:554:80:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f2:B:al.(2011), this aggregate elasticity is compatible with micro data, once we allow for intensive

28:1524:55041:22:21:58:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:production functions in real business cycle models because, in our environment, we have positive
28:1525:55137:21:22:58:553:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:proÖts that appear as capital income in the National Income and Product Accounts. Finally,

28:1528:55396:21:22:76:553:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The autoregressive parameter of the evolution of the response to ináation,-\r-, is set to 0.95.
28:1529:55491:22:22:58:553:591:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:In preliminary estimations, we discovered that the likelihood pushed this parameter to 1. When
28:1530:55585:22:21:58:553:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:this happened, the simulations became numerically unstable: after a series of positive innovations
28:1531:55683:21:22:58:553:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tolog\r-t, the reaction of nominal interest rates to ináation could be too tepid for too long. The
28:1532:55781:22:22:58:553:526:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:0.95 value seems to be the highest possible value of-\r-such that the problem does not appear.
28:1533:55875:22:21:58:553:504:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:The last two parameters,-\ryand-y;are equal to zero because, also in exploratory estimations,
28:1534:55968:21:22:58:553:483:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:B:the likelihood favored values of-y-0:Thus, we decided to forget about them and make\ry;t= 1:
28:1535:56060:22:22:76:554:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:To Önd the posterior, we proceed as follows. First, we deÖne a grid of parameter values and
28:1536:56151:22:21:58:553:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:check for the regions of high posterior density by evaluating the likelihood function in each point
28:1537:56250:21:22:58:553:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of the grid. This is a time-consuming procedure, but it ensures that we are searching in the right
28:1538:56348:22:22:58:553:396:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:zone of the parameter space. Once we have identiÖed the global maximum in the grid, we initialize
28:1539:56445:22:21:58:553:374:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a random-walk Metropolis-Hastings algorithm from this point. After an extensive Öne-tuning of
28:1540:56538:21:39:58:484:353:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the algorithm, we use 10,000 draws from the chain to compute posterior moments.

28:1566:57407:21:0:58:553:67:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:prices, which are reoptimized roughly once every Öve quarters, and in wages, which are reoptimized

29:1571:57886:22:21:58:553:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:model all prices and wages change every quarter. That is why, to a naive observer, our economy
29:1572:57980:21:22:58:358:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:would look like one displaying tremendous price áexibility.

29:1575:58227:21:22:58:553:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of consumption that match output growth and ináation áuctuations. The intratemporal shock
29:1576:58316:22:22:58:553:526:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is persistent to account for long-lived movements in hours worked. We estimate mean growth
29:1577:58406:22:21:58:553:504:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:rates of technology of 0.0034 (neutral) and 0.0028 (investment-speciÖc). Those numbers give us
29:1578:58500:21:22:58:553:483:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:an average growth of the economy of 0.44 percent per quarter, or around 1.77 percent on an
29:1579:58590:22:22:58:553:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:annual basis (0.46 and 1.86 percent in the data, respectively). Technology shocks, in our model,
29:1580:58686:22:21:58:553:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:are deviations with respect to these drifts. Thus, we estimate thatAtfalls in only 8 of the 192
29:1581:58781:21:22:58:553:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:quarters in our sample (which roughly corresponds to the percentage of quarters where measured
29:1582:58875:22:22:58:553:396:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:productivity falls in the data), even if we estimate negative innovations to neutral technology in
29:1583:58973:22:31:58:125:374:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:103 quarters.

30:1646:60872:21:22:76:553:416:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:In appendix 6.7 we plot the impulse response functions of the model implied by our estimates.
30:1647:60965:22:22:58:553:394:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:This exercise allows us to check that the estimates are sensible and that the behavior of the model
30:1648:61064:22:21:58:553:372:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is consistent with the behavior of related models in the literature. In appendix 6.8 we compare our
30:1649:61163:21:22:58:553:351:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:model against an alternative version without parameter drifting but still with stochastic volatility.
30:1650:61264:22:22:58:553:329:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:That is, we ask whether, once we have included stochastic volatility, it is still important to allow
30:1651:61364:22:21:58:553:307:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:for changes in the monetary policy rule to account for the time-varying volatility of U.S. aggregate
30:1652:61464:21:22:58:553:286:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:data over the last several decades. The results show that, even after controlling for stochastic
30:1653:61560:22:22:58:553:264:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:volatility, the data strongly prefer a speciÖcation where the monetary policy rule has changed over
30:1654:61659:22:21:58:553:242:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:time. In appendix 6.9 we show, though, that this Önding does not imply that volatility shocks did
30:1655:61756:21:22:58:553:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:not play an important role in the time-varying volatilities of U.S. aggregate time series. In other
30:1656:61855:22:22:58:553:199:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:words, both stochastic volatility and parameter drifting are key parts of a successful dynamic
30:1657:61949:22:27:58:261:177:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium model of the U.S. economy.
30:1658:61987:27:15:71:553:150:7:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:F:3Also, these second-order e§ects enormously complicate the introduction of time-variation in-. The likelihood
30:1659:62096:15:12:58:553:135:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:F:wants to match the moments of the ergodic distribution of ináation, not the level of-, which is ináation along
30:1660:62206:12:12:58:553:123:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:F:the balanced growth path. When we have non-linearities, the mean of that ergodic distribution may be far from
30:1661:62315:12:0:58:426:111:10:g_d0_f19:10:g_d0_f2:F:-:Thus, learning about-is hard. Learning about a time-varying-is even harder.

31:1713:63536:31:22:64:547:218:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:F:Figure 4.1: Smoothed intertemporal (logdt) shock, intratemporal (log't) shock, investment-speciÖc

31:1715:63720:30:21:76:553:166:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We see in the top left panel of Ögure 4.1 that the intertemporal shock,logdt;is particularly high
31:1716:63817:21:22:58:553:145:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in the 1970s. This increases householdsídesire for current consumption (for instance, because of
31:1717:63913:22:22:58:553:123:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the entrance of baby boomers into adulthood). A higher aggregate demand triggers, in the model,
31:1718:64008:22:21:58:553:101:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the higher ináation observed in the data for those years. The shock has a dramatic drop in the
31:1719:64102:21:22:58:553:80:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:second quarter of 1980. This is precisely the quarter in which the Carter administration invoked
31:1720:64198:22:0:58:553:58:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the Credit Control Act (March 14, 1980). Schreft (1990) documents that this measure caused
32:1721:64290:0:22:58:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:turmoil in Önancial markets and, most likely, distorted intertemporal choices of households, which
32:1722:64388:22:21:58:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is reáected in the large negative innovation tologdt. The low values oflogdtin the 1990s with
32:1723:64481:21:22:58:464:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:respect to the 1970s and 1980s eased the ináationary pressures in the economy.
32:1724:64559:22:22:76:553:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The shock to the utility of leisure,log't, grows in the 1970s and falls in the 1980s to stabilize
32:1725:64656:22:21:58:553:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:at a very low value in the 1990s. The likelihood wants to track, in this way, the path of average
32:1726:64753:21:22:58:553:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:hours worked: low in the 1970s, increasing in the 1980s, and stabilizing in the 1990s. Higher hours
32:1727:64852:22:22:58:553:591:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:also lower the marginal cost of Örms (wages fall relative to the technology level). The reduction
32:1728:64949:22:21:58:449:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in marginal costs also helped to reduce ináation during Greenspanís tenure.
32:1729:65024:21:22:76:553:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The evolution of the investment-speciÖc technology,loge-t, shows a sharp drop after 1973 (when
32:1730:65118:22:22:58:553:526:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:it is likely that energy-intensive capital goods su§ered the consequences of the oil shocks in the form
32:1731:65221:22:21:58:553:504:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of economic obsolescence) and large positive realizations in the late 1990s (our model interprets
32:1732:65318:21:22:58:553:483:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the sustained boom of those years as the consequence of strong improvements in investment
32:1733:65407:22:22:58:553:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:technology). These positive realizations were an additional help to contain ináation during the
32:1734:65502:22:21:58:553:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:1990s. In comparison, the neutral-technology shocks,logeAt, have been stable since 1959, with
32:1735:65595:21:22:58:299:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:only a few big shocks at the end of the sample.
32:1736:65642:22:22:76:553:396:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The evolution of the monetary policy shock,log-t, reveals large innovations in the early 1980s.
32:1737:65737:22:21:58:553:374:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:This is due both to the fast change in policy brought about by Volcker and to the fact that a Taylor
32:1738:65837:21:22:58:553:353:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:rule might not fully capture the dynamics of monetary policy during a period in which money
32:1739:65928:22:22:58:553:331:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:growth targeting was attempted. Sims and Zha (2006) also Önd that the Volcker period appears
32:1740:66020:22:21:58:553:309:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to be one with large disturbances to the policy rule and argue that the Taylor rule formalism can
32:1741:66117:21:22:58:553:288:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:be a misleading perspective from which to view policy during that time. Our evidence from the
32:1742:66210:22:22:58:553:266:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:estimated intertemporal, intratemporal, and investment shocks suggests that monetary authorities
32:1743:66306:22:21:58:479:244:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:faced a more di¢ cult environment in the 1970s and early 1980s than in the 1990s.
32:1744:66387:21:22:76:553:223:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:As a way to gauge the level of uncertainty of our smoothed estimates, we also plot in Ögure
32:1745:66478:22:22:58:553:201:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:4.1 the same shock (-2standard deviations). The lesson to take away from this Ögure is that, in
32:1746:66573:22:0:58:416:179:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:all cases, the data are informative about the history we just narrated.

33:1790:67359:34:22:76:553:351:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We move now, in Ögure 4.2, to plot the evolution of the volatility shocks, all of them in log-

33:1793:67643:21:22:58:553:286:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:1970s and only slowly went down during the 1980s and early 1990s. By the end of the sample,
33:1794:67734:22:22:58:553:264:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the standard deviation of the intertemporal shock was roughly at the level where it started. In

33:1796:67925:21:22:58:553:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:for a large drop in the standard deviation of the monetary policy shock in the early 1980s as
33:1797:68018:22:22:58:553:199:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:well as large changes in the standard deviation of the investment shock during the period of oil
33:1798:68114:22:21:58:553:177:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:price shocks. Hence, the 1970s and the 1980s were more volatile than the 1960s and the 1990s,
33:1799:68207:21:22:58:553:156:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:creating a tougher environment for monetary policy. This result also conÖrms Blanchard and
33:1800:68297:22:22:58:553:134:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Simonís (2001) and Nason and Smithís (2008) observation that volatility had a downward trend
33:1801:68389:22:21:58:553:112:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in the 20th century with an abrupt and temporal increase in the 1970s. Also, from the size of the
33:1802:68486:21:22:58:553:91:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:plus/minus two standard deviations, we conclude that the big movements in the di§erent series
33:1803:68579:22:0:58:434:69:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that we report can be ascertained with a reasonable degree of conÖdence.

34:1818:68817:223:34:58:553:438:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Figure 4.3: Smoothed path for the Taylor rule parameter on ináation +/- 2 standard deviations.
34:1819:68911:34:22:76:554:404:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, in Ögure 4.3, we plot the evolution of the response of monetary policy to ináation
34:1820:69002:22:22:58:553:382:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:plus/minus a two-standard-deviation interval. In particular, we graph\r-\r-t. This graph shows
34:1821:69096:22:21:58:553:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:us an intriguing narrative. The parameter started the sample around its estimated mean, slightly
34:1822:69192:21:22:58:553:339:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:over 1, and it grew more or less steadily during the 1960s until reaching a peak in early 1968.
34:1823:69287:22:22:58:553:317:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:After that year, it su§ered a fast collapse that took it below 1 in 1971. To put this evolution
34:1824:69382:22:21:58:553:295:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in perspective, it is useful to remember that Burns was appointed chairman in February 1970.
34:1825:69474:21:22:58:553:274:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:The parameter stayed below 1 for all of the 1970s. The arrival of Volcker is quickly picked up by
34:1826:69571:22:22:58:553:252:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:our smoothed estimates: it increases to over 2 after a few months and stays high during all the
34:1827:69666:22:21:58:553:230:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:years of Volckerís tenure. Interestingly, our estimate captures well the observation by Goodfriend
34:1828:69764:21:22:58:553:209:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and King (2007) that monetary policy tightened in the spring of 1980 as ináation and long-run
34:1829:69857:22:22:58:553:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ináation expectations continued to grow. Its level stayed roughly constant at this high during
34:1830:69951:22:22:58:553:165:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the remainder of Volckerís tenure. But as quickly as it rose when Volcker arrived, it went down
34:1831:70046:22:21:58:553:143:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:again when he departed. Greenspanís tenure at the Fed meant that, by 1990, the response of the
34:1832:70140:21:22:58:553:122:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monetary authority to ináation was again below 1. Moreover, our estimates are relatively tight.
34:1833:70235:22:22:58:553:100:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Fern·ndez-Villaverdeet al.(2010a) discuss how the results of the estimation relate to historical
34:1834:70331:22:0:58:105:78:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:evidence.
35:1835:70342:0:33:58:153:721:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:5. Conclusion
35:1836:70355:33:22:58:553:688:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:In this paper, we have shown how to estimate dynamic equilibrium models with stochastic volatil-
35:1837:70451:22:22:58:553:666:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ity. The key of the procedure is to realize that a second-order perturbation to the solution of this
35:1838:70551:22:21:58:553:644:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:class of models has a very particular structure that can be easily exploited to build an e¢ cient
35:1839:70648:21:22:58:553:623:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:particle Ölter. The recent boom in the literature on dynamic equilibrium models with stochastic
35:1840:70743:22:22:58:553:601:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:volatility suggests that this procedure may have many uses. Our characterization of the solution
35:1841:70839:22:22:58:553:579:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:might also be, on many occasions, of interest in itself to understand the dynamic properties of
35:1842:70934:22:21:58:444:557:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the equilibrium even if the researcher does not want to estimate the model.
35:1843:71009:21:22:76:553:536:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:As an application to illustrate how the procedure works we have estimated a business cycle
35:1844:71099:22:22:58:553:514:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:model with both stochastic volatility in the structural shocks that drive the economy and para-
35:1845:71194:22:21:58:553:492:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:meter drifting in the monetary policy rule. Such a model is motivated by the need to have an
35:1846:71286:21:22:58:553:471:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:empirical framework where we can account for the time-varying volatility of U.S. aggregate time
35:1847:71381:22:22:58:553:449:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:series. In particular, we have explained how you get point estimates in such a model and how
35:1848:71473:22:21:58:553:427:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to recover and analyze the smoothed structural and volatility shocks. Finally, through di§erent
35:1849:71568:21:22:58:553:406:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:comments -even if brief and not exhaustive- we have discussed the di§erent empirical lessons that
35:1850:71665:22:0:58:224:384:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:one can get from all those steps.

54:3340:97696:21:22:58:553:498:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the consequence of one variable (-t) being raised to another variable (\r-;t). Thus, the log-linear
54:3341:97795:22:40:58:241:476:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:approximation of the Taylor rule is:
54:3342:97831:40:0:139:145:436:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:f
54:3343:97832:0:11:148:155:450:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:-
54:3344:97833:11:0:158:260:439:12:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f5:C:bRt;bRt-1;b-t;b\r-;t;"mt
54:3345:97857:0:14:260:267:450:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:-
54:3346:97858:14:39:270:553:436:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:A:'bRt-\rRbRt-1-(1-\rR)\r-b-t+--"-t(50)
54:3347:97895:39:22:58:553:397:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:which does not depend on\r-;t;but only on the steady state\r-and it is exactly the same
54:3348:97982:22:22:58:553:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:expression as the one without parameter drifting. Hence, in order to capture parameter drifting
54:3349:98077:22:38:58:461:353:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in the Taylor rule, weneed, at least, to perform a second-order approximation.
54:3350:98155:38:29:58:161:315:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:6.4. Computation
54:3351:98171:29:22:58:553:286:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:In this section, we provide some more details regarding the computation of the paper. We generate
54:3352:98268:22:22:58:553:264:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:all the derivatives required by our second-order perturbation withMathematica6.0.  In that
54:3353:98358:22:21:58:553:242:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:way, we do not need to recompute the derivatives, the most time-intensive step, for each set of
54:3354:98453:21:22:58:553:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:parameter values in our estimation. Once we have all the relevant derivatives, we export them
54:3355:98546:22:22:58:553:199:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:automatically into Fortran Öles. This whole process takes about 3 hours. Then, we compile the
54:3356:98639:22:21:58:553:177:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:resulting Öles with theIntel Fortran Compilerversion10:1:025withIMSL. Previous versions
54:3357:98726:21:22:58:553:156:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:failed to compile our project because of the length of some of the expressions. Compilation takes
54:3358:98823:22:22:58:470:134:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:about18hours. The project has1798Öles and occupies2:33Gbytes of memory.
54:3359:98894:22:21:76:553:112:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The next step is, for given parameter values, to compute the Örst- and second-order approxi-
54:3360:98986:21:22:58:553:91:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:mation to the decision rules around the deterministic steady state using the analytic derivatives
54:3361:99083:22:0:58:553:69:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:we found before. For this task, Fortran takes around5seconds. Once we have the solution, we
55:3362:99176:0:22:58:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:approximate the likelihood using the particle Ölter with10;000particles. This number delivered
55:3363:99270:22:21:58:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a good compromise between accuracy and time to compute the likelihood. The evaluation of one
55:3364:99362:21:22:58:554:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:likelihood requires22seconds on a Dell server with 8 processors. Once we have the likelihood
55:3365:99454:22:22:58:553:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:evaluation, we guess new parameter values and we start again. This means that drawing 5,000
55:3366:99545:22:21:58:553:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:times from the posterior (even forgetting about the initial search over a grid of parameter values)
55:3367:99644:21:22:58:175:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:takes around 38 hours.
55:3368:99666:22:22:76:553:591:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:It is important to emphasize that theMathematicaandFortrancode were highly optimized
55:3369:99750:22:21:58:553:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in order to 1) keep the size of the project within reasonable dimensions (otherwise, the compiler
55:3370:99847:21:22:58:553:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:cannot parse the Öles and, even when it can, it delivers code that is too ine¢ cient) and 2) provide
55:3371:99947:22:22:58:245:526:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a fast computation of the likelihood.
55:3372:99984:22:21:76:553:504:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f17:A:Perhaps the most important task in that optimization was the parallelization of theFortran
55:3373:100074:21:22:58:553:483:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:code usingOPENMPas well as the compilation options:OG(global optimizations) andLoop Unroll.
55:3374:100165:22:22:58:553:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:In addition, we tailored specialized code to perform the matrix multiplications required in the Örst-
55:3375:100266:22:21:58:294:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and second-order terms of our model solution.
55:3376:100311:21:22:76:553:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Implementing corollary 1 requires the solution of a linear system of equations and the com-
55:3377:100402:22:22:58:553:396:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:putation of a Jacobian. For our particular application, we found that the following sequence of
55:3378:100497:22:30:58:306:374:12:g_d0_f17:12:g_d0_f2:B:LAPACKoperations delivered the fastest solution:
55:3379:100545:30:30:72:480:344:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:1.DGESV(computes the solution to a real system of linear equationsA-X=B).
55:3380:100618:30:31:72:553:314:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:2.DGETRI(computes the inverse of a matrix using the LU factorization from the previous line).
55:3381:100711:31:30:72:503:283:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:3.DGETRF(helps to compute the determinant of the inverse from the previous line).
55:3382:100792:30:22:76:554:253:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Without the parallelization and our optimized code, the solution of the model and evaluation
55:3383:100884:22:21:58:257:231:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of its likelihood take about70seconds.
55:3384:100922:21:22:76:553:210:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:With respect to the random-walk Metropolis-Hastings, we performed an intensive process of
55:3385:101011:22:22:58:553:188:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Öne-tuning of the chain, both in terms of initial conditions as well as in terms of getting the
55:3386:101106:22:21:58:553:166:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:right acceptance level. The only other important remark is to remember that as pointed out by
55:3387:101199:21:22:58:553:145:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:McFadden (1989) and Pakes and Pollard (1989), we must keep the random numbers used for
55:3388:101285:22:22:58:553:123:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:resampling in the particle Ölter constant across draws of the Markov chain. This is required to
55:3389:101380:22:21:58:553:101:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:achieve stochastic equi-continuity, and even if this condition is not strictly necessary in a Bayesian
55:3390:101482:21:22:58:553:80:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:framework, it reduces the numerical variance of the procedure, which was a serious concern for us
55:3391:101579:22:0:58:247:58:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:given the complexity of our problem.
56:3392:101617:0:29:58:208:721:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:6.5. Construction of Data
56:3393:101642:29:22:58:553:692:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:When we estimate the model, we make the series provided by the National Income and Product
56:3394:101732:22:22:58:553:670:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Accounts (NIPA) consistent with the deÖnition of variables in the theory. The main adjustment
56:3395:101825:22:21:58:553:648:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:we undertake is to express both real output and real gross investment in consumption units. Our
56:3396:101920:21:22:58:553:627:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:model implies that there is a numeraire in terms of which all the other prices need to be quoted.
56:3397:102017:22:22:58:553:605:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:We pick consumption as the numeraire. The NIPA, in comparison, uses an index of all prices
56:3398:102107:22:21:58:553:583:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to transform nominal GDP and investment into real values. In the presence of changing relative
56:3399:102201:21:22:58:553:562:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:prices, such as the ones we have seen in the U.S. over the last several decades with the fall in the
56:3400:102301:22:22:58:542:540:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:relative price of capital, NIPAís procedure biases the valuation of di§erent series in real terms.
56:3401:102399:22:21:76:553:518:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We map theory into the data by computing our own series of real output and real investment.
56:3402:102490:21:22:58:553:497:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:To do so, we use the relative price of investment, deÖned as the ratio of an investment deáator
56:3403:102585:22:22:58:553:475:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and a deáator for consumption. The denominator is easily derived from the deáators of non-
56:3404:102675:22:21:58:553:453:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:durable goods and services reported in the NIPA. It is more complicated to obtain the numerator
56:3405:102770:21:22:58:553:432:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:because, historically, NIPA investment deáators were poorly constructed. Instead, we rely on the
56:3406:102866:22:22:58:553:410:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:investment deáator computed by Fisher (2006). Since the series ends early in 2000.Q4, we have
56:3407:102959:22:21:58:356:388:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:extended it to 2007.Q1 by following Fisherís methodology.
56:3408:103016:21:22:76:554:367:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:For the real output per capita series, we Örst deÖne nominal output as nominal consumption
56:3409:103106:22:22:58:553:345:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:plus nominal gross investment. We deÖne nominal consumption as the sum of personal consump-
56:3410:103197:22:21:58:553:323:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tion expenditures on non-durable goods and services.  We deÖne nominal gross investment as
56:3411:103287:21:22:58:553:302:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the sum of personal consumption expenditures on durable goods, private residential investment,
56:3412:103381:22:22:58:553:280:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and non-residential Öxed investment. Per capita nominal output is equal to the ratio between
56:3413:103473:22:21:58:553:258:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:our nominal output series and the civilian non-institutional population between 16 and 65. To
56:3414:103566:21:22:58:553:237:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:obtain per capita values, we divide the previous series by the civilian non-institutional population
56:3415:103666:22:22:58:553:215:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:between 16 and 65. Finally, real wages are deÖned as compensation per hour in the non-farm
56:3416:103756:22:38:58:282:193:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:business sector divided by the CPI deáator.
56:3417:103799:38:30:58:249:155:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:6.6. Determinacy of Equilibrium
56:3418:103830:30:21:58:553:125:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:We mentioned in the main text that the estimated value of\r-(1.045 in levels) guarantees local
56:3419:103924:21:22:58:553:104:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:determinacy of the equilibrium. To see this note that, for local determinacy, the relevant part
56:3420:104019:22:22:58:553:82:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of the solution of the model isonlythe linear, Örst-order component. This component depends
56:3421:104110:22:0:58:553:60:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:on\r-, the mean policy response, and not on the current value of\r-t. The economic intuition is
57:3422:104207:0:22:58:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that local unicity survives even if\r-ttemporarily violates the Taylor principle as long as there is
57:3423:104307:22:21:58:552:699:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:B:reversion to the mean in the policy response and, thus, the agents have the expectation that\r-t
57:3424:104403:21:22:58:553:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:will satisfy the Taylor principle on average. For a related result in models with Markov-switching
57:3425:104501:22:22:58:553:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:regime changes, see Davig and Leeper (2006).  While we cannot Önd an analytical expression
57:3426:104591:22:21:58:553:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:for the determinacy region, numerical experiments show that, conditional on the other point
57:3427:104682:21:22:58:553:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:estimates, values of\r-above 0.98 ensure uniqueness. Since the likelihood assigns zero probability
57:3428:104780:22:22:58:553:591:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to values of\r-lower than 1.01, well inside the determinacy region, multiplicity of local equilibria
57:3429:104880:22:38:58:229:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is not an issue in our application.
57:3430:104915:38:29:58:250:531:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:6.7. Impulse Response Functions
57:3431:104946:29:22:58:553:502:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:As a check of our estimates, we plot the IRFs generated by the model to a monetary policy shock.
57:3432:105042:22:22:58:553:480:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:This exercise is an important test. If the IRFs match the shapes and sizes of those gathered
57:3433:105134:22:21:58:553:458:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:by time series methods such as SVARs, it will strengthen our belief in the rest of our results.
57:3434:105229:21:22:58:442:437:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Otherwise, we should at least understand where the di§erences come from.
57:3435:105301:22:22:76:554:415:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Auspiciously, the answer is positive: our model generates dynamic responses that are close to
57:3436:105394:22:21:58:553:393:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the ones from SVARs (see, for instance, Sims and Zha, 2006). The left panel of Ögure 6.1 plots the
57:3437:105492:21:22:58:553:372:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:IRFs to a monetary shock of three variables commonly discussed in monetary models: the federal
57:3438:105586:22:22:58:553:350:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:funds rate, output growth, and ináation. Since we have a non-linear model, in all the Ögures in
57:3439:105681:22:21:58:553:328:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:this section, we report the generalized IRFs starting from the mean of the ergodic distribution
57:3440:105776:21:22:58:553:307:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(Koop, Pesaran, and Potter, 1996). After a one-standard-deviation shock to the federal funds
57:3441:105868:22:22:58:553:285:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:rate, ináation goes down in a hump-shaped pattern for many quarters and output growth drops.
57:3442:105960:22:21:76:553:263:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The right panel of Ögure 6.1 plots the IRFs after a one-standard-deviation innovation to the
57:3443:106052:21:22:58:553:242:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monetary policy shock computed conditional on Öxing\r-tto the estimated mean during the tenure
57:3444:106146:22:22:58:553:220:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of each of three di§erent chairmen of the Board of Governors: the combination Burns-Miller,
57:3445:106237:22:21:58:553:198:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Volcker, and Greenspan. This exercise tells us how the variation on the systematic component
57:3446:106329:21:22:58:553:177:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of monetary policy has a§ected the dynamics of aggregate variables. Furthermore, it allows a
57:3447:106421:22:22:58:553:155:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:comparison with numerous similar exercises done in the literature with SVARs where the IRFs
57:3448:106512:22:21:58:254:133:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:are estimated on di§erent subsamples.
57:3449:106549:21:22:76:553:112:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The most interesting di§erence is that the response of output growth under Volcker was the
57:3450:106639:22:22:58:553:90:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:mildest: the estimated average stance of monetary policy under his tenure reduces the volatility
57:3451:106735:22:0:58:553:68:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of output. Ináation responds moderately as well since the agents have the expectation that future
58:3452:106834:0:22:58:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shocks will be smoothed out by the monetary authority.  This Önding also explains why the
58:3453:106923:22:21:58:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:IRFs of the interest rate are nearly on top of each other for all three periods: while we estimate
58:3454:107021:21:22:58:553:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that monetary policy responded more during Volckerís years for any given level of ináation than
58:3455:107116:22:22:58:553:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:under Burns-Miller or Greenspan, this policy lowers ináation deviations and hence moderates the
58:3456:107211:22:21:58:553:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:actual movement along the equilibrium path of the economy. Moreover, this second set of IRFs
58:3457:107303:21:22:58:553:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:already points out one important result of this paper: we estimate that monetary policy under
58:3458:107396:22:22:58:553:591:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Burns-Miller and Greenspan was similar, while it was di§erent under Volcker. This Önding will
58:3459:107489:22:285:58:410:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:be reinforced by the results we present in the main body of the text.

61:3673:112577:21:22:58:553:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is conventionally considered overwhelming evidence in favor of the model with parameter drift
61:3674:112670:22:22:58:553:526:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(Je§reys, 1961, for instance, suggests that di§erences bigger than 5 are decisive). Thus, even after
61:3675:112770:22:21:58:553:504:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:controlling for stochastic volatility, the data strongly prefer a speciÖcation where monetary policy
61:3676:112870:21:22:58:553:483:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:has changed over time. This Önding, however, does not imply that volatility shocks did not play
61:3677:112965:22:22:58:553:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:an important role in the time-varying volatilities of U.S. aggregate time series. In fact, as we will
61:3678:113066:22:21:58:516:439:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:B:see in the next section of this appendix, they were a key mechanism in accounting for it.4
61:3679:113156:21:22:76:553:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:It has been noted that the estimation of log MDDs is dangerous because of numerical insta-
61:3680:113246:22:22:58:553:396:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bilities in the evaluation of the integral log marginal data density (log MDD). This concern is
61:3681:113341:22:21:58:553:374:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:particularly relevant in our case, since we have a large model saddled with burdensome computa-
61:3682:113436:21:22:58:553:353:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tion. Thus, as a robustness analysis, we also computed the Bayesian Information Criterion (BIC)
61:3683:113531:22:22:58:553:331:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(Schwarz, 1978). The BIC, which avoids the need to handle the integral in the log MDD, can be
61:3684:113624:22:21:58:553:309:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:understood as an asymptotic approximation of the Bayes factor that also automatically penalizes
61:3685:113719:21:40:58:328:288:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:for extra parameters. The BIC of modeliis deÖned:
61:3686:113768:40:0:196:274:248:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:BICi=-2 lnp
61:3687:113779:0:10:276:281:258:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:-
61:3688:113780:10:0:282:365:248:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:C:YT=Ydata;T;b\r;i
61:3689:113796:0:10:365:370:258:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:-
61:3690:113797:10:40:373:415:248:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f6:C:+kilnn
61:3691:113803:40:21:58:553:208:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:whereb\ris the maximum likelihood estimator (or, given our áat priors, the mode of the posterior),
61:3692:113901:21:27:58:553:187:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f2:B:kiis the number of parameters, andnis the number of observations. Then, the BIC of the model
61:3693:113993:27:16:71:553:160:7:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:F:4A formal comparison with the case without stochastic volatility is more di¢ cult, since we are taking advantage
61:3694:114105:16:12:58:553:144:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:F:of its presence to evaluate the likelihood. Fortunately, Justiniano and Primiceri (2008) and Fern·ndez-Villaverde
61:3695:114218:12:12:58:553:132:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:F:and Rubio-RamÌrez (2007) estimate models similar to ours with and without stochastic volatility (in the Örst case,
61:3696:114332:12:12:58:553:120:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:F:using only a Örst-order approximation to the decision rules of the agents and in the second with measurement
61:3697:114440:12:12:58:553:108:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:F:errors). Both papers Önd that the Öt of the model improves substantially when we include stochastic volatility. Fi-
61:3698:114555:12:12:58:553:96:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:F:nally, Fern·ndez-Villaverde and Rubio-RamÌrez (2008) compare a model with parameter drifting and no stochastic
61:3699:114665:12:12:58:553:84:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:F:volatility with a model without parameter drifting and no stochastic volatility and report that parameter drifting
61:3700:114779:12:0:58:245:72:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:F:is also strongly preferred by the likelihood.
62:3701:114826:0:22:58:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:B:with stochastic volatility and parameter drifting isBICdrift=-2-3885 + 28-ln 192 =-7;622:8:
