62:3705:115196:22:38:58:293:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in favor of the model with parameter drifting.
62:3706:115242:38:29:58:238:596:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:6.9. Historical Counterfactuals
62:3707:115273:29:22:58:553:567:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:One important additional exercise is to quantify how much of the observed changes in the volatil-
62:3708:115370:22:22:58:553:545:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ity of aggregate U.S. variables can be accounted for by changes in the standard deviations of
62:3709:115463:22:21:58:553:523:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shocks and how much by changes in policy. To accomplish this, we build a number of historical
62:3710:115556:21:22:58:553:502:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:counterfactuals. In these exercises, we remove one source of variation at a time and we measure
62:3711:115651:22:22:58:553:480:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:how aggregate variables would have behaved when hit only by the remaining shocks. Since our
62:3712:115742:22:21:58:553:458:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:model is structural in the sense of Hurwicz (1962) (it is invariant to interventions, including shocks
62:3713:115844:21:22:58:553:437:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:by nature such as the ones we are postulating), we will obtain an answer that is robust to the
62:3714:115938:22:22:58:133:415:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Lucas critique.
62:3715:115953:22:21:76:554:393:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:In the next two subsections, we will always plot the same three basic variables that we used in
62:3716:116048:21:22:58:553:372:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:section 4 of the main text: ináation, output growth, and the federal funds rate. Counterfactual
62:3717:116143:22:22:58:553:350:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:histories of other variables could be built analogously. Also, we will have vertical bars for the
62:3718:116240:22:38:58:432:328:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tenure of each chairman, following the same color scheme as in section 4.
62:3719:116313:38:30:58:319:290:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:6.9.1. Counterfactual I: Switching Chairmen
62:3720:116356:30:21:58:553:260:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:In our Örst counterfactual, we move one chairman from his mandate to an alternative time period.
62:3721:116452:21:22:58:553:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:For example, we appoint Greenspan as chairman during the Burns-Miller years. By that, we mean
62:3722:116545:22:22:58:553:217:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that the Fed would have followed the policy rule dictated by the average\r-testimated during
62:3723:116637:22:21:58:553:195:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Greenspanís time while starting from the same states as Burns-Miller and su§ering the same
62:3724:116727:21:22:58:553:174:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shocks (both structural and of volatility).  We repeat this exercise with all the other possible
62:3725:116823:22:22:58:553:152:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:combinations: Volcker in the Burns-Miller decade, Burns-Miller in Volckerís mandate, Greenspan
62:3726:116917:22:21:58:553:130:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in Volckerís time, Burns-Miller in the Greenspan years, and, Önally, Volcker in Greenspanís time.
62:3727:117014:21:22:76:553:109:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:It is important to be careful in interpreting this exercise. By appointing Greenspan at Volckerís
62:3728:117111:22:22:58:553:87:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:time, we do not literally mean Greenspan as a person, but Greenspan as a convenient label for a
62:3729:117206:22:0:58:553:65:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:particular monetary policy response to shocks that according to our model were observed during
63:3730:117302:0:22:58:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:his tenure. The real Greenspan could have behaved in a di§erent way, for example, as a result of
63:3731:117398:22:21:58:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:some non-linearities in monetary policy that are not properly captured by a simple rule such as the
63:3732:117497:21:22:58:553:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:one postulated in section 3. The argument could be pushed one step further and we could think
63:3733:117590:22:22:58:553:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:about the appointment of Volcker as an endogenous response of the political-economic equilibrium
63:3734:117686:22:21:58:553:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to high ináation. In our model agents have a probability distribution regarding possible changes in
63:3735:117785:21:22:58:553:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monetary policy in the next periods, but those changes are uncorrelated with current conditions.
63:3736:117881:22:22:58:430:591:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Therefore, our model cannot capture the endogeneity of policy selection.
63:3737:117953:22:21:76:553:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Another issue that we sidelined is the evolution of expectations. In our model, agents have
63:3738:118044:21:22:58:553:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:rational expectations and observe the changes in monetary policy parameters. This hypothesis
63:3739:118136:22:22:58:553:526:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:may be a poor approximation of the agentsíbehavior in real life. It could be the case that\r-twas
63:3740:118233:22:21:58:553:504:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:high in 1984, even though ináation was already low by that time, because of the high ináationary
63:3741:118329:21:22:58:553:483:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:expectations that economic agents held during most of the 1980s (this point is also linked to issues
63:3742:118429:22:22:58:553:461:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of commitment and credibility that our model does not address). While we see all these arguments
63:3743:118525:22:38:58:537:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:as interesting lines of research, we Önd it important to focus Örst on our basic counterfactual.
63:3744:118621:38:22:58:553:401:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f2:B:MomentsIn table 6.1, we report the mean and the standard deviation of ináation, output
63:3745:118707:22:21:58:553:379:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:growth, and the federal funds rate in the observed and in the sets of counterfactual data. Ináation
63:3746:118806:21:22:58:553:358:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:was high with Burns-Miller, fell with Volcker, and stayed low with Greenspan. Output growth
63:3747:118897:22:22:58:553:336:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:went down during the Volcker years to recover with Greenspan. The federal funds rate reached its
63:3748:118993:22:21:58:553:314:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:peak with Volcker. The standard deviation of output growth fell from 4.7 in Burns-Millerís time
63:3749:119088:21:22:58:553:293:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to 2.45 with Greenspan, a cut in half. Similarly, ináation volatility fell nearly 54 percent and the
63:3750:119188:22:22:58:252:271:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:federal funds rate volatility 5 percent.
63:3751:119228:22:21:76:554:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:But table 6.1 also tells us one important result: time-varying monetary policy signiÖcantly
63:3752:119319:21:22:58:553:228:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a§ected average ináation. In particular, Volckerís response to ináation was strong and switching
63:3753:119415:22:22:58:553:206:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:him to either Burns-Millerís or Greenspanís time would have reduced average ináation dramati-
63:3754:119508:22:21:58:553:184:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:cally. But it also tells us other things: contrary to the conventional wisdom, our estimates suggest
63:3755:119608:21:22:58:553:163:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that the stance of monetary policy against ináation under Greenspan was not strong. In Burns-
63:3756:119701:22:22:58:553:141:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Millerís time, the monetary policy under Greenspan would have delivered slightly higher average
63:3757:119796:22:21:58:553:119:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ináation, 6.83 versus the observed 6.23, accompanied by a lower federal funds rate and lower out-
63:3758:119893:21:22:58:553:98:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:put growth, 1.89 versus the observed 2.03. The di§erence is even bigger in Volckerís time, during
63:3759:119990:22:0:58:553:76:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:which average ináation would have been nearly 1.4 percent higher, while output growth would
64:3760:120083:0:22:58:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:have been virtually identical (1.34 versus 1.38). The key for this Önding is in the behavior of the
64:3761:120182:22:21:58:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:federal funds rate, which would have increased only by 9 basis points, on average, if Greenspan
64:3762:120277:21:22:58:553:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:had been in charge of the Fed instead of Volcker. Given the higher ináation in the counterfactual,
64:3763:120375:22:22:58:553:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the higher nominal interest rates would have meant much lower real rates. The counterfactual
64:3764:120467:22:21:58:553:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of Burns-Miller in Greenspanís and Volckerís time casts doubt on the malignant reputations of
64:3765:120560:21:22:58:553:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:these two short-lived chairmen, at least when compared with Greenspan. Burns-Miller would have
64:3766:120654:22:22:58:553:591:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:brought even slightly lower ináation than Greenspan, thanks to a higher real federal funds rate
64:3767:120749:22:21:58:553:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and a bit higher output growth. However, Burns-Miller would have delivered higher ináation than
64:3768:120844:21:29:58:99:548:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Volcker.

67:3966:124796:29:22:58:553:248:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:In our second historical counterfactual, we compute how the economy would have performed in
67:3967:124887:22:21:58:553:226:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the absence of changes in the volatility of the shocks, that is, if the volatility of the innovation of

67:3969:125084:22:22:58:553:183:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:structural shocks as we did in section 4.7 and we feed them to the model, given our parameter
67:3970:125177:22:21:58:553:161:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:point estimates and the historical mean of volatility, to generate series for ináation, output, and
67:3971:125276:21:39:58:171:140:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the federal funds rate.
67:3972:125299:39:21:58:553:101:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f2:B:MomentsTable 6.2 reports the moments of the data (in annualized terms) and the moments
67:3973:125385:21:22:58:553:80:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:from the counterfactual history (no s.v.in the table stands for ìno stochastic volatilityî). In both
67:3974:125485:22:0:58:553:58:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:cases, we include the moments for the whole sample and for the sample divided before and after
68:3975:125581:0:22:58:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:1984.Q1, a conventional date for the start of the great moderation (McConnell and PÈrez-QuirÛs,
68:3976:125676:22:21:58:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:2000). In the last two rows of the table, we compute the ratio of the moments after 1984.Q1 over
68:3977:125772:21:22:58:553:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the moments before 1984.Q1. The benchmark model with stochastic volatility plus parameter

68:4001:126872:26:21:76:553:231:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The table also reáects the fact that without volatility shocks, the reduction in volatility ob-
68:4002:126967:21:22:58:553:210:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:served after 1984 would have been noticeably smaller. The standard deviation of ináation would
68:4003:127061:22:22:58:553:188:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:have fallen by only 13 percent, the standard deviation of output growth would have fallen by 16
68:4004:127156:22:21:58:553:166:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:percent, and the standard deviation of the federal funds rate would have fallen by 35 percent, that
68:4005:127255:21:22:58:553:145:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is, only 33, 20, and 87 percent, respectively, of how much they would have fallen otherwise. We
68:4006:127350:22:22:58:553:123:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:must resist here the temptation to undertake a standard variance decomposition exercise. Since
68:4007:127444:22:21:58:553:101:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:we have a second-order approximation to the policy function and its associated cross-product
68:4008:127536:21:22:58:553:80:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:terms, we cannot neatly divide total variance among the di§erent shocks as we could do in the
68:4009:127629:22:0:58:115:58:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:linear case.
69:4010:127643:0:22:76:553:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Table 6.2 documents that, while time-varying policy is reáected in changes of average ináa-
69:4011:127734:22:21:58:553:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tion, volatility shocks a§ect the standard deviation of the observed series. Without time-varying
69:4012:127831:21:22:58:553:678:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:volatility the decrease in observed volatility would not have been nearly as big as we observed
69:4013:127926:22:22:58:553:656:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in the data. Hence, while changes in the systematic component of monetary policy account for
69:4014:128018:22:21:58:553:634:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:changes in average ináation, volatility shocks account for changes in the standard deviation of
69:4015:128113:21:22:58:553:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ináation, output growth and interest rates observed after 1984. Also, without stochastic volatility,
69:4016:128213:22:38:58:342:591:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:output growth would have been quite lower on average.
69:4017:128266:38:22:58:553:553:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f2:B:Counterfactual PathsFigure 6.7 compares the whole path of the counterfactual history (blue
69:4018:128356:22:22:58:553:531:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:line) with the observed one (red line). Figure 6.7 tells us that volatility shocks mattered throughout
69:4019:128458:22:21:58:553:509:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the sample. The run-up in ináation would have been much slower in the late 1960s (ináation would
69:4020:128554:21:22:58:553:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:have actually been negative during the last years of Martinís tenure) with small e§ects on output
69:4021:128651:22:22:58:553:466:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:growth or the federal funds rate (except at the very end of the sample).  Ináation would not
69:4022:128743:22:21:58:553:444:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:have picked up nearly as much during the Örst oil shock, but output growth would have su§ered.
69:4023:128837:21:22:58:553:423:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:During Volckerís time, ináation would also have fallen faster with little cost to output growth.
69:4024:128933:22:22:58:553:401:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:These are indications that both Burns-Miller and Volcker su§ered from large and volatile shocks
69:4025:129028:22:21:58:553:379:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to the economy. In comparison, during the 1990s, ináation would have been more volatile, with a
69:4026:129123:21:22:58:553:358:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:big increase in the middle of the decade. Similarly, during those years, output growth would have
69:4027:129220:22:22:58:553:336:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:been much lower, with a long recession between 1994 and 1998, and the federal funds rate would
69:4028:129314:22:21:58:553:314:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:have been prominently higher. ConÖrming the results presented in section 4 of the paper, this is
69:4029:129410:21:0:58:417:293:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:another manifestation of how placid the 1990s were for policy makers.
